Book of Purification. Our companions mentioned it in fiqh books according to their habit. In Fath al-Qadir: Our shaykhs mentioned something from Anas and Khudri, but the deficiency of our sight hid it from us. Shaykh Ala al-Din said: al-Tahawi narrated them from chains, and his student Imam al-Zayla'i al-Mukharrij followed him saying I did not find them in Sharh al-Athar of al-Tahawi, but he narrated from Hammad ibn Abi Sulayman that he said concerning a chicken that fell into a well and died: draw from it forty or fifty buckets. al-Muhaqqiq Siraj al-Hindi answered: it is possible that al-Tahawi mentioned them in his book Ikhtilaf al-Ulama or in Ahkam al-Quran or in another book, and lack of finding in al-Athar does not necessitate absolute non-existence. Third: the hadith of al-Zanji concerning the well of Zamzam, and we will discuss it if Allah wills. There is disagreement in the interpretation of the middle bucket: some say it is the bucket used in every city, and some say the consideration is the bucket of each well because the predecessors, when they used the term, it referred to the customary. This was chosen in al-Muhit, al-Ikhtiyar, al-Hidayah and others, and it is the apparent riwaya because it is mentioned in al-Kafi of al-Hakim. And some say it contains eight ratls, some say ten ratls, and other views. What appears is that the well either has a bucket or not; if it has a bucket, it is considered by it, otherwise a bucket containing the apparent is used as in al-Khulasa, Sharh al-Tahawi, and al-Siraj al-Wahhaj. Then one should interpret the view of those who specified a bucket as being when the well has no bucket, as is not hidden. If one draws the required amount according to its bucket or their buckets with one large bucket, it suffices and its purification is ruled, and that is the apparent madhhab. al-Hasan ibn Ziyad used to say: it is not purified except by drawing the required estimated buckets because by repeating the drawing, water springs and is taken from its top, so it becomes like flowing water, and this is not obtained by one bucket even if large. So in al-Bada'i', and it is transmitted in al-Tabyin and al-Nihaya from Zufr. We said: the purpose has been achieved, which is removing the required amount, about a sa' by a sa', from its bottom. The fourth is thirty and the fifth is forty. It should not escape you that twenty among those narrations is the middle between the few and the many because the few is three and seven, and the many is thirty and forty, and twenty is the middle between them. Contemplate well, you will obtain the result of reflection. End of Fara'id. His saying: (al-Mukharrij) meaning the author of Takhrij Ahadith al-Hidayah, cautioning against Imam al-Zayla'i the commentator of al-Kanz, for he is other than him. His saying: (And it is said: the consideration is the bucket of each well) its apparent is that it is an interpretation of the middle, but it is not; rather it is opposed to it. He said in al-Bada'i': then there is disagreement concerning the bucket: some said the consideration is the bucket of each well used to draw from it, whether small or large. And it is narrated from Abu Hanifa that he estimated a sa'. And some said the consideration is the middle between the small and the large. End. And the commentator al-Zayla'i said: the middle is the bucket used in every city, and some said the consideration is the bucket of each well because it is easier for them, and some said it contains a sa'. Contemplate. His saying: (Then one should interpret the view of those who specified a bucket) He said in al-Nahr: I say: the estimation by a sa' is based on the choice that it is the middle; and according to the interpretation of it as the bucket used in every city, it should be considered also for the one lacking it. So the conclusion is that whoever considers the bucket of each well, the consideration of the middle does not apply except for those without a bucket, and then the middle is considered according to both views. By this it is known that such an interpretation has no need. End. He meant by the two views: the view that the middle is a sa' and the view that the middle is used in every city. His saying: (with one large bucket) al-Ramli said: I say: if its customary bucket is very large, is the mentioned number required or is it sufficient? The apparent is the second, so it restricts their statement: the consideration is the bucket of each well. This is what the insight of the faqih requires, and by it it is known that the buckets used in the wells of our country's villages for cows, donkeys, and camels, called in our custom 'al-mahs', are of this type. Contemplate. His saying: (and it branches from the non-requirement of continuity) is a branching. al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 18 P/1
Source pages p. 208

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is an expansion on the rulings of nazh (drawing water from a well) when an animal dies in it. The author discusses the interpretation of 'al-dalw al-wast' (the middle bucket), which is key to determining the required number of buckets. There are multiple opinions: (1) it is the bucket commonly used in that city, (2) it is the specific bucket of that well, (3) it is a fixed measure like a sa' (about 8-10 ratls). The relied-upon view (zahir al-riwaya) is that the bucket of each well is considered, as chosen in al-Hidayah. The passage also addresses whether drawing with one large bucket suffices. al-Hasan ibn Ziyad and Zufr held that multiple smaller buckets are needed to achieve the effect of water flowing (like a stream), but the majority says the purpose is removal of the required quantity, so one large bucket suffices. The author also mentions the required numbers: for a mouse (fa'ra) 20 buckets, a chicken (dajaja) 30, a pigeon (hamama) 40, and so on. The twenty is considered 'middle' between low and high estimates. The discussion includes a clarification of the term 'al-mukharrij' and the views of later scholars like al-Ramli regarding very large buckets in village wells.

Key Terms
الدلو الوسط (al-dalw al-wast): The bucket used for drawing water from a well; its size is determined by local custom or the well's own bucket.
نزح (nazh): Drawing water from a well for purification after an impurity falls in.
توالي (tawali): Continuity in drawing water without significant breaks.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the relied-upon definition of 'al-dalw al-wast' in the Hanafi school according to the passage?
A) A bucket that holds 10 ratls.
B) The bucket of each well.
C) A medium-sized bucket.
D) The bucket used in every city.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school relies on the removal of the wajib quantity for well purification, using the well's own bucket size, without requiring continuity.

Ruling on Equivalent of Mouse and Condition of Continuity in Nazh
Explains ruling for mouse-equivalent animals and whether continuity is required in drawing water

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that continuity (tawali) is not required in nazh and identify that animals equivalent to a mouse are ruled by indication (dalala) rather than analogy.

Core Idea
Continuity not required in nazh; only remaining amount needed if well refills.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq addresses two key points: the non-requirement of continuity in drawing water from a well (nazh), and the method of extending the ruling from explicitly mentioned animals to similar ones. The author clarifies that you can draw water over multiple days and that animals similar to a mouse are included by textual indication, not by analogy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling on continuity
Find the statement that continuity is not required and the reason given.
The text says 'لا يشترط التوالي'.
2
Understand the application when well refills
Consider the case where partial nazh is done and water increases the next day.
Two opinions mentioned; the chosen view is to draw only the remaining amount.
3
Examine the method of extending rulings to similar animals
The author discusses whether the ruling for a mouse is extended to similar-sized animals by qiyas or dalala.
The preferred explanation is dalala (indication), not qiyas.
4
Analyze the objection and response
The objection is that well rulings are based on texts, so analogizing to other animals weakens the principle. The response shows how once a principle is established, it becomes a basis for further rulings.
Al-Bahr al-Raiq prefers the dalala explanation over the response in al-Mustasfa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فأره وأربعون بنحو حمامة وكله بنحو شاة وانتفاخ حيوان أو تفسخه ومائتان لو لم واعتبار معنى الجريان ساقط ولهذا لا يشترط التوالي في النزح حتى لو نزح في كل يوم دلو جاز، ويتفرع على عدم اشتراط التوالي أنه إذا نزح البعض ثم ازداد في الغد، وقيل ينزح كله، وقيل مقدار البقية. هذا مع أن في اشتراط التوالي خلافاً نقله في معراج الدراية لكن المختار عدم اشتراطه وأنه إذا ازداد في اليوم الثاني لا ينزح إلا ما بقي. إليه أشار في الخلاصة. وأشار المصنف رحمه الله بقوله بموت نحو «فارة إلى أن ما يعادل الفأرة في الجثة حكمه حكمها وأورد عليه سؤالاً وجواباً في المستصفى فقال : فإن قيل قد أن مسائل الآبار مر مبنية على اتباع الآثار والنص ورد في الفأرة والدجاجة والآدمي وقد قيس ما عادلها بها قلنا : بعد ما استحكم هذا الأصل صار كالذي ثبت على وقف القياس في حق التفريع عليه كما في الإجارة وسائر العقود التي يأبى القياس جوازها ا ولا يخفى ما فيه فإنه ظاهر في أن للرأي مدخلاً في بعض مسائل الآبار وليس كذلك فالأولى أن يقال: إن هذا إلحاق بطريق الدلالة لا بالقياس كما اختاره في معراج الدراية.
A mouse and forty [buckets] for like a pigeon and all [water] for like a sheep, and swelling of an animal or its decomposition, and two hundred if not. And consideration of the meaning of running [water] is void, and for this reason continuity is not required in drawing water, so that if he drew one bucket each day it is permissible. And it branches from the non-requirement of continuity that if he draws some then the next day the water increases, it is said he draws all, and it is said [he draws] the amount of the remainder. This, while there is disagreement regarding requiring continuity as transmitted in Mi'raj al-Diraya, but the chosen view is not requiring it, and that if it increases on the second day, he only draws what remains. This is indicated in al-Khulasa. And the author (rahimahullah) indicated by his saying 'by the death of a mouse' that whatever equals a mouse in the body has its ruling. And he stated a question and answer in al-Mustasfa, saying: If it is said that the issues of wells are built upon following the narrations and text, and the text came regarding the mouse, chicken, and human, and what equals them has been measured by them, we say: After this principle became firm, it became like that which is established upon stopping analogy with respect to deriving branches, as in ijarah and all contracts whose permissibility analogy rejects. And it is not hidden that there is something in it, for it is clear that opinion has an entry in some issues of wells, and it is not so. So it is better to say: This is annexation by way of indication, not by analogy, as chosen in Mi'raj al-Diraya.
Source pages p. 209

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling for animals that are equivalent to a mouse (fara) in size when they die in a well. The author states that the condition of continuity (tawali) in drawing water is not required; you can draw one bucket each day and it suffices. If after drawing some water the well refills the next day, you only need to draw the remaining required amount, not all over again. This is the relied-upon position. The text also addresses an objection: that well rulings are based on textual evidence (athar) for specific animals like mouse, chicken, human, but other animals are included by qiyas (analogy). The response given in al-Mustasfa is that once the principle is established, it becomes like a fixed rule upon which further branches are built, similar to contracts like ijarah where analogy is not used initially. However, the author of al-Bahr al-Raiq finds this unsatisfactory and prefers to say it is annexation by 'dalala' (indication) rather than qiyas.

Key Terms
نزح (nazh): Drawing water from a well, especially to remove impurity.
توالي (tawali): Continuity; doing an act without interruption.
فأرة (fa'rah): A mouse; the smallest animal for which a specific nazh amount is prescribed (20 buckets wajib, 10 mustahabb).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In Hanafi fiqh, if a mouse dies in a well and the owner draws 10 buckets today and 10 buckets tomorrow, is this valid?
A) No, because continuity is required
B) Yes, because continuity is not required
C) Only if the well is completely emptied
D) No, because 20 buckets must be drawn in one day

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school does not require continuity in nazh, and animals similar to the mouse are included by textual indication (dalala) rather than analogy.

Mustahabb Amounts for Single Animals and the Difference in Imam Muhammad's Statements
Discusses recommended amounts and resolves conflicting narrations from Imam Muhammad.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended amounts for a mouse and a chicken based on Imam Muhammad's statements and explain why the lower amount (10) is considered more apparent.

Core Idea
The recommended amount for a mouse is 10 buckets, not 20, because al-Jami' al-Saghir's narration outweighs al-Asl.

In the previous lesson, we learned the obligatory amounts for nazh. Now we turn to the recommended (mustahabb) amounts. The base text (Kanz al-Daqaiq) does not mention these, but scholars inferred them from Imam Muhammad's expressions. Interestingly, Imam Muhammad himself gave different numbers in different works, leading to an intra-madhhab discussion. This lesson unpacks that discussion and shows how later Hanafi scholars resolved it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
What is the mustahabb amount for a mouse? Note that the text gives two numbers: 10 and 20.
The mustahabb is additional to the wajib amount.
2
Trace the source of each number
20 is from al-Asl, 10 is from al-Jami' al-Saghir.
Both are works of Imam Muhammad.
3
Apply the Hanafi principle for conflicting narrations
The later work (al-Jami' al-Saghir) takes precedence over the earlier (al-Asl).
This is based on the principle that the later statement is more mature.
4
Understand the reasoning
Some argued that the higher number is due to animal size, but the preferred view is based on narration.
Ghayat al-Bayan confirms the priority of narration.
5
Conclude the mufta bihi
The mustahabb for a mouse is 10 buckets.
This is the operative ruling for fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وأربعون بنحو حمامة) أي ينزح أربعون دلواً وسطاً بموت نحو حمامة وقد تقدم دليله قريباً، وقد ذكر المصنف في هذين النوعين القدر الواجب ولم يذكر المستحب ولم يتعرض له الشارح الزيلعي أيضاً، والمذكور في غيرهما أن المستحب في نحو الفأرة عشرة، وفي نحو الدجاجة اختلف كلام محمد في الأصل والجامع الصغير؛ ففي الأصل ما يفيد أن المستحب عشرون، وفي الجامع الصغير عشرة قال في الهداية وهو الأظهر. وعلل له في غاية البيان بأن الجامع الصغير صنف بعد الأصل فأفاد أن الظهور من جهة الرواية لا من جهة الدراية . وقد يقال من جهة الدراية إن الذي يضعف بسبب كبر الحيوان إنما هو الواجب لا المستحب. واعلم أن القدر المستحب المذكور لم يصرح به في ظاهر الرواية وإنما فهمه بعض المشايخ من عبارة محمد رحمه الله حيث قال : ينزح في الفأرة عشرون أو ثلاثون، وفي الهرة أربعون أو خمسون فلم يرد به التخيير بل أراد به بيان الواجب والمستحب، وليس هذا الفهم بلازم بل يحتمل أنه إنما قال ذلك لاختلاف الحيوانات في الصغر والكبر ففي الصغير ينزح الأقل، وفي الكبير ينزح الأكثر . وقد اختار هذا بعضهم كما نقله في البدائع، ولعل هذا هو الصواب. قوله : (ويتفرع على عدم اشتراط التوالي الخ) التفريع سبب ترك التعرض للمستحب في الكتاب، ثم هذا إذا كان الواقع واحداً، فأما إذا تعدد فالفأرتان إذا لم يكونا كهيئة الدجاجة كفارة واحدة إجماعاً، وكذا إذا كانا كهيئة الدجاجة إلا فيما روي عن محمد أنه ينزح منها أربعون والهرتان كالشاة إجماعاً. وجعل أبو يوسف الثلاث والأربع كفارة واحدة والخمسة كالهرة إلى التسع والعشرة كالكلب. وقال محمد: الثلاث كالهرة، والست كالكلب ولم يوجد التصحيح في كثير من الكتب لكن في المبسوط أن ظاهر الرواية أن الثلاث كالهرة فيفيد أن الست كالكلب وبه يترجح قول محمد «وما كان بين الفأرة والهرة فحكمه حكم الفأرة، وما كان بين الهرة والكلب فحكمه حكم الهرة». وهكذا يكون حكم الأصغر والهرة مع الفأرة كالهرة ويدخل الأقل في الأكثر. كذا في التنجيس وغيره. وظاهره يخالف قول من قال إن الفأرة إذا كانت هاربة من الهرة فوقعت في البئر وماتت ينزح جميع الماء لأنها تبول غالباً فإن على هذا القول يجب نزح الجميع في الهرة مع الفأرة لأنها تبول خوفاً، قد جزم به جماعة لكن قال في المجتبى : وقيل بخلافه وعليه الفتوى ولعل وجهه أن في ثبوت كونها بالت شكاً فلا يثبت بالشك.
His saying: (And forty for like a pigeon) i.e., forty medium buckets are drawn for the death of something like a pigeon, and its proof was given recently. The author mentioned in these two types the obligatory amount and did not mention the recommended, nor did the commentator Zayla'i address it. But it is mentioned elsewhere that the recommended for something like a mouse is ten, and for something like a chicken the statement of Muhammad differs between al-Asl and al-Jami' al-Saghir: in al-Asl it indicates that the recommended is twenty, and in al-Jami' al-Saghir ten. Al-Hidayah says it (the latter) is more apparent. It is explained in Ghayat al-Bayan that al-Jami' al-Saghir was written after al-Asl, so it indicates that the preference is by way of narration, not by opinion. And it may be said from the view of opinion that what decreases due to the size of the animal is only the obligatory, not the recommended. Know that the recommended amount mentioned is not explicitly stated in the apparent narration, but some scholars understood it from the statement of Muhammad (rahimahullah) where he said: 'Twenty or thirty are drawn for a mouse, and forty or fifty for a cat' — he did not mean choice but rather to explain the obligatory and the recommended. But this understanding is not necessary; rather it is possible that he said that due to the difference of animals in smallness and largeness, so for the small one the less is drawn, and for the large one the more. And some chose this as transmitted in al-Bada'i', and perhaps this is correct. His saying: (And it branches from the non-requirement of continuity...) The branching is the reason for leaving out the recommended in the book. Then this is if the occurrence is single. As for multiplicity, two mice if they are not like the size of a chicken are one expiation (kaffarah) by consensus, and likewise if they are like the size of a chicken except what is reported from Muhammad that forty are drawn for them. And two cats are like a sheep by consensus. Abu Yusuf made three and four as one expiation, and five like a cat up to nine, and ten like a dog. Muhammad said: three are like a cat, and six like a dog. And correction is not found in many books, but in al-Mabsut it is the apparent narration that three are like a cat, and it implies that six are like a dog, and by this the statement of Muhammad is preponderant. 'And what is between a mouse and a cat has the ruling of a mouse, and what is between a cat and a dog has the ruling of a cat.' And thus the ruling of the smaller with the cat is like the cat, and the smaller is included in the larger. As in al-Tanjis and others. And its apparent contradicts the statement of one who says that if a mouse is fleeing from a cat and falls into a well and dies, all water is drawn because she usually urinates; for according to this view, drawing all would be obligatory for a cat with a mouse because she urinates out of fear. Some were certain of this, but in al-Mujtaba it is said: 'It is said otherwise, and upon it is the fatwa', and perhaps its basis is that there is doubt about her urinating, so it is not established by doubt.
Source pages p. 209

Commentary
This passage discusses the recommended (mustahabb) amounts for drawing water when animals die in a well. The author notes that the base text only mentions the obligatory amounts, not the recommended. The recommended for a mouse is 10 or 20 buckets depending on the source. Imam Muhammad's statements in al-Asl and al-Jami' al-Saghir differ, with the latter (10) being more relied upon. The passage then discusses multiple animals. If two mice die, the ruling depends on their combined size. Abu Yusuf categorized groups: three or four animals count as one 'kaffarah' (expiation), five to nine as a cat, ten as a dog. Muhammad said three is like a cat, six like a dog. The apparent narration supports Muhammad. For an animal between sizes, the ruling follows the smaller category. There is also a discussion about a mouse fleeing from a cat: if it falls in and dies, some say the cat's fear causes urination requiring full drawing, but the fatwa is otherwise due to doubt.

Key Terms
مستحب (mustahabb): Recommended act; doing it is rewarded but not obligatory.
كفارة (kaffarah): Expiation; here it refers to the required nazh amount for multiple animals, as if one ruling covers them all.
هرة (hirah): A cat; a medium-sized animal for which 40 buckets are wajib.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preponderant Hanafi view, what is the mustahabb amount for a mouse that dies in a well?
A) 20 buckets
B) 10 buckets
C) 30 buckets
D) 5 buckets

Key Takeaway
The mustahabb amount for a mouse is 10 buckets, derived from Imam Muhammad's later work, showing the importance of riwayah order.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Multiple Animal Deaths: Abu Yusuf vs. Muhammad
Discusses intra-Hanafi dispute on grouping multiple animal deaths.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between Abu Yusuf's and Muhammad's categorizations for multiple animal deaths in a well and apply the preponderant view (Muhammad's) to determine the required number of buckets.

Core Idea
For multiple animals, Abu Yusuf uses a gradual scale; Muhammad uses fixed thresholds; Muhammad's view is preponderant.

When multiple animals die in a well, the ruling differs depending on whether they are considered together or separately. The Hanafi school has an internal disagreement between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad on how to categorize groups of small animals. This lesson examines their respective systems and identifies the relied-upon position.

Guided Path
1
Understand the consensus
Two mice = one mouse ruling; two cats = one sheep ruling. These points are agreed upon.
Consensus (ijma') exists on these points within the Hanafi school.
2
Note the difference in thresholds
For three mice, Abu Yusuf says it's one kaffarah (like one mouse?), while Muhammad says it's like a cat (40 buckets).
The practical difference starts at three small animals.
3
Diagram Abu Yusuf's scale
Groups: 3-4 = 1 kaffarah, 5-9 = like a cat (40), 10 = like a dog (all water).
This is a progressive scale based on number.
4
Diagram Muhammad's scale
Groups: 3 = like a cat (40), 6 = like a dog (all water). Numbers in between follow the smaller rule (e.g., 4 and 5 follow the mouse rule? Actually, text says 'what is between mouse and cat follows mouse' so 4 and 5 would be like mouse? But Muhammad only sets thresholds at 3 and 6. The text says 'وما كان بين الفأرة والهرة فحكمه حكم الفأرة' so for numbers between 1 and 3? Wait need careful: The phrase means: what is between mouse and cat in size has the ruling of mouse. So for multiple animals, the combined size matters. But the dispute is about number. Actually the passage says: 'وجعل أبو يوسف الثلاث والأربع كفارة واحدة والخمسة كالهرة إلى التسع والعشرة كالكلب. وقال محمد: الثلاث كالهرة، والست كالكلب'. So Muhammad's scale is more discrete: only 3 and 6 specified, others presumably follow the principle of the smaller? The text then says: 'وما كان بين الفأرة والهرة فحكمه حكم الفأرة' which seems to be a general principle. For groups, it might mean that if the combined size is between a mouse and cat, it's like a mouse. But the dispute is about number counting, not size. We need to be precise. The passage later talks about 'والهرة مع الفأرة كالهرة' meaning the larger dominates. So for groups, the ruling depends on the larger animal's category. However, the dispute is about how many animals equal a cat or dog. So the guided path should reflect that.
Muhammad's view is more specific and supported by al-Mabsut.
5
Apply the tarjih
Al-Mabsut supports Muhammad, so his view is mufta bihi.
This is the basis for fatwa.

قوله : (وأربعون بنحو حمامة) أي ينزح أربعون دلواً وسطاً بموت نحو حمامة وقد تقدم دليله قريباً، وقد ذكر المصنف في هذين النوعين القدر الواجب ولم يذكر المستحب ولم يتعرض له الشارح الزيلعي أيضاً، والمذكور في غيرهما أن المستحب في نحو الفأرة عشرة، وفي نحو الدجاجة اختلف كلام محمد في الأصل والجامع الصغير؛ ففي الأصل ما يفيد أن المستحب عشرون، وفي الجامع الصغير عشرة قال في الهداية وهو الأظهر. وعلل له في غاية البيان بأن الجامع الصغير صنف بعد الأصل فأفاد أن الظهور من جهة الرواية لا من جهة الدراية . وقد يقال من جهة الدراية إن الذي يضعف بسبب كبر الحيوان إنما هو الواجب لا المستحب. واعلم أن القدر المستحب المذكور لم يصرح به في ظاهر الرواية وإنما فهمه بعض المشايخ من عبارة محمد رحمه الله حيث قال : ينزح في الفأرة عشرون أو ثلاثون، وفي الهرة أربعون أو خمسون فلم يرد به التخيير بل أراد به بيان الواجب والمستحب، وليس هذا الفهم بلازم بل يحتمل أنه إنما قال ذلك لاختلاف الحيوانات في الصغر والكبر ففي الصغير ينزح الأقل، وفي الكبير ينزح الأكثر . وقد اختار هذا بعضهم كما نقله في البدائع، ولعل هذا هو الصواب. قوله : (ويتفرع على عدم اشتراط التوالي الخ) التفريع سبب ترك التعرض للمستحب في الكتاب، ثم هذا إذا كان الواقع واحداً، فأما إذا تعدد فالفأرتان إذا لم يكونا كهيئة الدجاجة كفارة واحدة إجماعاً، وكذا إذا كانا كهيئة الدجاجة إلا فيما روي عن محمد أنه ينزح منها أربعون والهرتان كالشاة إجماعاً. وجعل أبو يوسف الثلاث والأربع كفارة واحدة والخمسة كالهرة إلى التسع والعشرة كالكلب. وقال محمد: الثلاث كالهرة، والست كالكلب ولم يوجد التصحيح في كثير من الكتب لكن في المبسوط أن ظاهر الرواية أن الثلاث كالهرة فيفيد أن الست كالكلب وبه يترجح قول محمد «وما كان بين الفأرة والهرة فحكمه حكم الفأرة، وما كان بين الهرة والكلب فحكمه حكم الهرة». وهكذا يكون حكم الأصغر والهرة مع الفأرة كالهرة ويدخل الأقل في الأكثر. كذا في التنجيس وغيره. وظاهره يخالف قول من قال إن الفأرة إذا كانت هاربة من الهرة فوقعت في البئر وماتت ينزح جميع الماء لأنها تبول غالباً فإن على هذا القول يجب نزح الجميع في الهرة مع الفأرة لأنها تبول خوفاً، قد جزم به جماعة لكن قال في المجتبى : وقيل بخلافه وعليه الفتوى ولعل وجهه أن في ثبوت كونها بالت شكاً فلا يثبت بالشك.
His saying: (And forty for like a pigeon) i.e., forty medium buckets are drawn for the death of something like a pigeon, and its proof was given recently. The author mentioned in these two types the obligatory amount and did not mention the recommended, nor did the commentator Zayla'i address it. But it is mentioned elsewhere that the recommended for something like a mouse is ten, and for something like a chicken the statement of Muhammad differs between al-Asl and al-Jami' al-Saghir: in al-Asl it indicates that the recommended is twenty, and in al-Jami' al-Saghir ten. Al-Hidayah says it (the latter) is more apparent. It is explained in Ghayat al-Bayan that al-Jami' al-Saghir was written after al-Asl, so it indicates that the preference is by way of narration, not by opinion. And it may be said from the view of opinion that what decreases due to the size of the animal is only the obligatory, not the recommended. Know that the recommended amount mentioned is not explicitly stated in the apparent narration, but some scholars understood it from the statement of Muhammad (rahimahullah) where he said: 'Twenty or thirty are drawn for a mouse, and forty or fifty for a cat' — he did not mean choice but rather to explain the obligatory and the recommended. But this understanding is not necessary; rather it is possible that he said that due to the difference of animals in smallness and largeness, so for the small one the less is drawn, and for the large one the more. And some chose this as transmitted in al-Bada'i', and perhaps this is correct. His saying: (And it branches from the non-requirement of continuity...) The branching is the reason for leaving out the recommended in the book. Then this is if the occurrence is single. As for multiplicity, two mice if they are not like the size of a chicken are one expiation (kaffarah) by consensus, and likewise if they are like the size of a chicken except what is reported from Muhammad that forty are drawn for them. And two cats are like a sheep by consensus. Abu Yusuf made three and four as one expiation, and five like a cat up to nine, and ten like a dog. Muhammad said: three are like a cat, and six like a dog. And correction is not found in many books, but in al-Mabsut it is the apparent narration that three are like a cat, and it implies that six are like a dog, and by this the statement of Muhammad is preponderant. 'And what is between a mouse and a cat has the ruling of a mouse, and what is between a cat and a dog has the ruling of a cat.' And thus the ruling of the smaller with the cat is like the cat, and the smaller is included in the larger. As in al-Tanjis and others. And its apparent contradicts the statement of one who says that if a mouse is fleeing from a cat and falls into a well and dies, all water is drawn because she usually urinates; for according to this view, drawing all would be obligatory for a cat with a mouse because she urinates out of fear. Some were certain of this, but in al-Mujtaba it is said: 'It is said otherwise, and upon it is the fatwa', and perhaps its basis is that there is doubt about her urinating, so it is not established by doubt.
Source pages p. 209

Commentary
This passage discusses the recommended (mustahabb) amounts for drawing water when animals die in a well. The author notes that the base text only mentions the obligatory amounts, not the recommended. The recommended for a mouse is 10 or 20 buckets depending on the source. Imam Muhammad's statements in al-Asl and al-Jami' al-Saghir differ, with the latter (10) being more relied upon. The passage then discusses multiple animals. If two mice die, the ruling depends on their combined size. Abu Yusuf categorized groups: three or four animals count as one 'kaffarah' (expiation), five to nine as a cat, ten as a dog. Muhammad said three is like a cat, six like a dog. The apparent narration supports Muhammad. For an animal between sizes, the ruling follows the smaller category. There is also a discussion about a mouse fleeing from a cat: if it falls in and dies, some say the cat's fear causes urination requiring full drawing, but the fatwa is otherwise due to doubt.

Key Terms
مستحب (mustahabb): Recommended act; doing it is rewarded but not obligatory.
كفارة (kaffarah): Expiation; here it refers to the required nazh amount for multiple animals, as if one ruling covers them all.
هرة (hirah): A cat; a medium-sized animal for which 40 buckets are wajib.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi view, how many buckets are drawn for six mice that die together in a well?
A) 20 buckets
B) 40 buckets
C) All water
D) 30 buckets

Key Takeaway
In multiple animal deaths, the relied-upon view is that three is like a cat (40 buckets), six is like a dog (all water), and smaller numbers follow the mouse ruling.

Ruling for Sheep-Sized Animals in Wells: Evidence from Zamzam
Explanation of the ruling for sheep-equivalent animals with a Companions' proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for drawing well water when a sheep-sized animal dies, and identify the Companion-based evidence from the Zamzam incident.

Core Idea
A human or dog in a well requires drawing all water—proved by the Companions' action in Zamzam.

In Hanafi fiqh, when an animal the size of a sheep or larger dies in a well, all the water must be drawn out. This ruling applies regardless of whether the animal is considered pure (like a human) or impure (like a dog). The primary evidence comes from an incident in the well of Zamzam, where two Companions, Ibn Abbas and Ibn Zubayr, ordered the entire well to be emptied after an Ethiopian died in it. In this lesson, we will examine that evidence and how it establishes the ruling for all comparable animals.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its scope
Read the opening statement: 'all water is drawn for what equals a sheep in the body, like a human and a dog, whether pure or impure.' Note the benchmark (sheep-sized) and that purity is irrelevant.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the fatwa of Ibn Abbas and Ibn Zubayr in the Zamzam incident, narrated by Muhammad ibn Sirin via Daraqutni. Identify that this is a Companion action (qawl sahabi) transmitted as an ahad narration.
Thubut: zanni; Dalala: qati because command is clear.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The Companions ordered drawing all water for a human. The illa is the body mass comparable to a sheep. Thus, any animal of similar size requires the same.
The ruling extends to dogs and other animals of that size.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some may restrict the ruling to humans, but the Hanafi school applies it to all sheep-sized animals. Also, note the intra-Hanafi dispute on exact water amounts for cats and dogs (Muhammad vs Abu Yusuf).
The mufta bihi is to draw all water for sheep-sized.
5
Consider scenario details
The passage also addresses a cat-and-mouse case: if both die, 40 buckets; if only mouse, 20; if mouse urinates, all water. This reinforces the proportionality.
These furu derive from the same principle.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وكله بنحو شاة) أي ينزح ماء البئر كله بموت ما عادل الشاة في الجثة كالآدمي والكلب، طاهراً كان أو نجساً، لأن ابن عباس وابن الزبير أفتيا بنزح الماء كله حين مات زنجي في بئر زمزم كما رواه ابن سيرين وعطاء وعمر وبن دينار وقتادة وأبو الطفيل، أما رواية ابن سيرين فأخرجها الدارقطني في سننه بإسناده عن محمد بن سيرين أن زنجياً مات في زمزم فأمر به ابن عباس فأخرج وأمر بها أن تنزح قال : فغلبتهم عين جاءت من الركن قال فأمر بها فسدت بالقباطي والمطارف حتى نزحوها، فلما نزحوها انفجرت عليهم. والقباطي جميع قبطية وهو ثوب من ثياب مصر رقيقة بيضاء وكأنه منسوب إلى القبط وهم أهل مصر، للقول الثاني فقط . قوله : ولعل هذا الخ قال في النهر : هذا الاحتمال ساقط لما مر من أن مسائل الآبار بنيت على الآثار والوارد فيما أسست به محمد رحمه الله إنما هو إيجاب العشرين في نحو الفأرة، والأربعين في نحو الفأرة، والأربعين في نحو الحمامة مطلقاً، ولو صح هذا الاحتمال لبطل ذلك الاستدلال ولهذا تعين حمل كلام محمد على ما فهمه المشايخ قوله : (وبه يترجح قول محمد) أقول : وكذا جزم به في متن المواهب فقال : وألحق أي محمد الثلاث منها إلى الخمس بالهرة، والست بالكلب لا الخمس إلى التسع بها والعشر به اهـ. أي ما ألحق الخمس إلى التسع بالهرة والعشر بالكلب كما قاله أبو يوسف قوله : وظاهره يخالف قول من قال الخ) قال في النهر أقول: لا يلزم من كونها معها أن تكون هاربة منها والتقييد بموتها غير واقع لما مر . ثم رأيت في السراج قال : لو أن هرة أخذت فأرة فوقعتا جميعاً في البئر إن أخرجتا حيتين لم ينزح شيء، أو ميتين نزح أربعون، أو الفأرة ميتة فقط فعشرون، وإن مجروحة أو بالت نزح جميع الماء اهـ . وهو حسن موافق لما في المجتبى. وبقي من الأقسام موت الهرة فقط، ولا شك في وجوب نزح الأربعين قوله : (ولعل وجهه الخ) قال في
His saying: (and all [water] for like a sheep) i.e., all the water of the well is drawn for the death of what equals a sheep in the body, like a human and a dog, whether pure or impure, because Ibn Abbas and Ibn Zubayr gave a fatwa to draw all the water when an Ethiopian died in the well of Zamzam, as narrated by Ibn Sirin, Ata', Umar, Ibn Dinar, Qatada, and Abu al-Tufayl. As for the narration of Ibn Sirin, al-Daraqutni recorded it in his Sunan with his chain from Muhammad ibn Sirin that an Ethiopian died in Zamzam, and Ibn Abbas ordered him to be removed and ordered that it be drawn. He said: 'Then they were overcome by a spring that came from the corner.' He said: 'So he ordered it to be plugged with qibati and matarif until they drew it. When they drew it, it burst upon them.' Qibati is the plural of qibtiyya, a thin white garment from Egypt, apparently attributed to the Copts, the people of Egypt. For the second opinion only. His saying: (And perhaps this...) Al-Nahr said: This probability is invalid because, as has passed, well issues are built on narrations, and what has been transmitted that Muhammad (rahimahullah) established is only the obligation of twenty for something like a mouse, and forty for something like a mouse [?], and forty for something like a pigeon absolutely. If this probability were correct, that deduction would be invalid, hence it is necessary to interpret Muhammad's statement as the scholars understood. His saying: (And by this the statement of Muhammad is preponderant) I say: and similarly it is asserted in the text of al-Mawahib, saying: Muhammad annexed three to five with the cat, and six with the dog, not five to nine with it and ten with it as Abu Yusuf said. His saying: (And its apparent contradicts the statement of one who said...) Al-Nahr said: I say: it does not follow from her being with it that she is fleeing from it, and the restriction to her death is not happening as previously. Then I saw in al-Siraj he said: If a cat took a mouse and both fell into the well, if they are taken out alive, nothing is drawn; if both dead, forty are drawn; if only the mouse is dead, twenty; and if it is wounded or urinates, all water is drawn. This is good and agrees with what is in al-Mujtaba. There remains the death of the cat alone, and there is no doubt about the obligation of drawing forty. His saying: (And perhaps its basis...) Source pages p. 210

Commentary
This passage covers the ruling for animals the size of a sheep or larger: all water must be drawn. The author provides evidence from the incident in Zamzam where Ibn Abbas and Ibn Zubayr ordered the entire well to be emptied after an Ethiopian (a human) died in it. The narration from Ibn Sirin is given, including details of how they plugged the well with cloth until they could draw it. The passage then continues with clarifications on earlier disputes: it reaffirms that Muhammad's view (three to five = cat, six = dog) is preponderant over Abu Yusuf's. It also addresses a situation where a cat and mouse fall together: determining the cause of death and potential urination matters. The fatwa is that if the mouse is wounded or urinates, all water is drawn; otherwise, the standard amounts apply. The commentary ends with noting that for a cat alone, forty buckets are wajib.

Key Terms
زنجي (zinji): An Ethiopian (or black African) person; used in the narration of the Zamzam incident.
شاة (shah): A sheep; used as a benchmark for size in well rulings.

Key Terms from Source Passage

According to the passage, what is the primary evidence for drawing all water when a sheep-sized animal dies in a well?

B) The fatwa of Ibn Abbas and Ibn Zubayr in the Zamzam incident.
C) Analogy from the ruling for a mouse.
D) Consensus of the four schools.

Key Takeaway
For any animal equal to or larger than a sheep in body mass, all water must be drawn from the well, based on the Companions' action in Zamzam.

Large Animal Carcasses in Wells: The Zamzam Proof
Establishing the ruling that a sheep-sized carcass requires drawing all well water

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a sheep-sized carcass in a well, cite the Zamzam incident as evidence, and explain why the Hanafi school upholds its authenticity.

Core Idea
Death of a sheep-sized animal in a well makes all water impure – full drawing is wajib.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq establishes a central Hanafi ruling on well purification: when an animal the size of a sheep or larger dies in a well, all water must be drawn out. The proof is the famous incident of a black man dying in the well of Zamzam, where Ibn Abbas and Ibn al-Zubayr ordered complete emptying. The commentator then defends this narration against authenticity and interpretation challenges raised by the Shafi'i school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling and Its Condition
Pinpoint the exact ruling: wajib to draw all well water when an animal with a body mass equal to or larger than a sheep (including human, dog) dies in it, whether the animal is pure or impure.
The ruling applies to any creature meeting the size threshold, regardless of ritual purity.
2
Locate the Dalil
The evidence is the practice of the Companions: when a black man died in Zamzam, Ibn Abbas and Ibn al-Zubayr ordered the entire well emptied. Multiple transmission paths are listed (Ibn Sirin, Ata', Amr ibn Dinar, Qatada, Abu al-Tufayl).
The hadith is ahad but accepted due to multiple corroborations.
3
Analyse the Objections
The Shafi'i school raised issues: transmissions are mursal, some narrators weak, Sufyan ibn Uyayna and al-Shafi'i denied knowledge of the incident, and they suggested the drawing was for cleaning, not impurity.
Objections target both authenticity and interpretation.
4
Trace the Hanafi Defence
The commentator argues that mursal narrations are acceptable when the intermediary is trustworthy (e.g., Ikrima); the criticized narrators like Jabir al-Ju'fi and Ibn Lahi'a are considered trustworthy by many; and positive evidence by other imams outweighs lack of knowledge of Sufyan and al-Shafi'i. The apparent wording indicates impurity.
The principle: اثبات مقدم على نفي (established proof precedes denial).
5
Evaluate the Thamarah al-Khilaf
Practical consequence: Hanafi school requires full drawing for any sheep-sized carcass; Shafi'i school requires no drawing unless water changes in color, taste, or smell.
This difference affects daily practice in well maintenance.

حديث الزنجي الذي قالوا إنه وقع في بئر زمزم، ولا سمعت أحداً يقول نزحت زمزم. ثم أسند عن الشافعي أنه قال : لا يعرف هذا عن ابن عباس، وكيف يروي ابن عباس عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم «الماء لا ينجسه شيء لم يعرفا فقد عرف غيرهما ممن ذكرناه من الإعلام الأئمة وإثباتهم مقدم على نفي غيرهم مع أن بينهما وبين ذلك الوقت قريباً من مائة وخمسين سنة. وأما رواية ابن عباس الماء لا ينجسه شيء» فيجوز أن يكون وقع عنده He said: 'And all water due to something like a sheep' means all the water of the well is drawn due to the death of something equal to a sheep in body, like a human and a dog, whether pure or impure, because Ibn Abbas and Ibn al-Zubayr gave a fatwa to draw all the water when a black man died in the well of Zamzam, as narrated by Ibn Sirin, Ata', Amr ibn Dinar, Qatada, and Abu al-Tufayl. As for the narration of Ibn Sirin, al-Daraqutni extracted it in his Sunan with his chain from Muhammad ibn Sirin that a black man died in Zamzam, so Ibn Abbas ordered him to be taken out and ordered the water to be drawn. He said: 'Then a spring from the corner overcame them; he ordered that it be blocked with Egyptian garments and mufflers until they drew it, and when they drew it, it burst upon them.' (Explanation of terms). As for the narration of Ata', Ibn Abi Shayba narrated it in his Musannaf and al-Tahawi in Sharh al-Athar that an Ethiopian fell into the well of Zamzam and died, so Ibn al-Zubayr ordered its water drawn, but the water did not stop; then he saw a spring flowing from near the Black Stone, and Ibn al-Zubayr said, 'That is enough for you.' As for the narration of Amr ibn Dinar, al-Bayhaqi narrated it, and the one ordering the drawing was Ibn Abbas. As for the narration of Qatada, Ibn Abi Shayba narrated it in his Musannaf, and the order was by Ibn Abbas. As for the narration of Abu al-Tufayl, al-Bayhaqi narrated it, and the order was by Ibn Abbas. Then if they say that the narration of Ibn Sirin is mursal because he did not meet Ibn Abbas but heard it from Ikrima, and similarly Qatada did not meet Ibn Abbas; and the narration of Ibn Dinar includes Ibn Lahi'a, who is not acceptable as evidence; and the narration of Abu al-Tufayl includes Jabir al-Ju'fi, who is not acceptable; and Ata' heard from Ibn al-Zubayr without disagreement, but there is something that weakens his narration, which is what al-Bayhaqi narrated from Sufyan ibn Uyayna that he said: 'I have been in Mecca for seventy years, I have never seen a young or old person knowing the hadith of the black man who they say fell into Zamzam, nor have I heard anyone say that Zamzam was drawn.' Then he narrated from al-Shafi'i that he said: 'This is not known from Ibn Abbas; how can Ibn Abbas narrate from the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'Water is not made impure by anything' and then act contrary? If he did do it, it was due to impurity appearing on the surface of the water or for cleaning, not due to impurity, because Zamzam is for drinking.' The answer: since Ibn Sirin sent (mursal) from Ibn Abbas and the intermediary between them was trustworthy, i.e., Ikrima, the hadith is authentic and acceptable as evidence. In al-Tamhid by Ibn Abd al-Barr, the mursal narrations of Ibn Sirin are considered strong and authentic like the mursal narrations of Sa'id ibn al-Musayyib. As for al-Ju'fi, al-Thawri and Shu'ba declared him trustworthy, people accepted him and narrated from him, and no one differed about narrating from him; al-Tahawi also narrated from him. As for Ibn Lahi'a, Ibn Adi said: He is good in hadith, his hadith is written, and trustworthy people like al-Thawri, Shu'ba, Amr ibn al-Harith, and Layth ibn Sa'd narrated from him. The lack of knowledge of Sufyan and al-Shafi'i is not a valid argument in the religion of Allah; established proof takes precedence over denial. If they did not know, others who are the notable imams we mentioned did know, and their established evidence takes precedence over denial, especially since between them and that time there was nearly 150 years. As for the narration of Ibn Abbas (water is not made impure by anything), it is possible that he had evidence that necessitated its specification; his narration is like knowledge of the opponent of it, just as al-Shafi'i (may Allah have mercy on him) said regarding less than two qullas without change due to another evidence that specified this hadith for him, not for Ibn Abbas. As for the suggestion that the drawing was due to impurity appearing or for cleaning, it contradicts the apparent meaning, because the apparent meaning of the saying 'he died and he ordered its drawing' is that it was due to death, not another impurity, just as they say 'he committed adultery and was stoned', 'he forgot and prostrated', 'he stole and was cut off', especially since according to them, water is not drawn due to impurity. If it were for cleaning, he would not have ordered its drawing, and they would not have gone to such great lengths to block the spring. And the statement of al-Nawawi: 'How can this...'
Source pages p. 210

Commentary
This passage comments on the phrase 'and all water due to something like a sheep' from the matn. The commentator explains that the death of any animal or being with a body mass equal to or greater than a sheep, such as a human or dog, requires drawing all the water from the well, regardless of whether the animal was pure or impure. The proof is the practice of the Companions Ibn Abbas and Ibn al-Zubayr when a black man died in the well of Zamzam. Multiple narrations are cited. The commentator then addresses objections to the authenticity of these reports. The objections include that the narrations are mursal, that some narrators are weak, and that Sufyan ibn Uyayna and al-Shafi'i denied knowledge of the incident. The commentator defends the hadith by noting that the intermediaries are trustworthy, that mursal reports of Ibn Sirin are accepted by many scholars, and that the denials of Sufyan and al-Shafi'i are outweighed by the positive attestations of other imams. The commentator also refutes the interpretation that the drawing was for cleaning, arguing that the apparent wording indicates it was due to the death causing impurity. This reasoning solidifies the Hanafi position that large animal carcasses necessitate complete emptying of the well.

Key Terms
شاة (shāh): Sheep; used as the threshold for a large animal carcass that requires drawing all well water.
نزح (nazh): Drawing water from a well; here, complete emptying for large carcasses.
زمزم (Zamzam): The well in Mecca; historically cited as a case for drawing all water due to a human death.
مرسل (mursal): A hadith where the Companion is omitted; the commentator argues such narrations are acceptable when the transmitter is trustworthy.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires complete emptying of a well when any animal with a body mass equal to or larger than a sheep dies in it, relying on the authentic practice of the Companions in the Zamzam incident.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate
8 min
Ruling on Bloating or Disintegration of Animals in Well Water
Explains ruling and branches for well purification when animal falls in

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for a well when an animal bloats or disintegrates, apply the branching rules for pumping amounts, and distinguish the positions of Muhammad and Abu Yusuf in cases of pouring impure water.

Core Idea
Bloating or disintegration of an animal in a well requires pumping all its water because liquid impurity spreads like a drop of wine.

When an animal falls into a well and remains until it bloats or disintegrates, the water becomes impure due to the separating liquid impurity. The Hanafi school establishes that all water must be pumped out, regardless of the animal's size. This lesson explores the ruling, its reason, and the practical branches (furu'ah) that address special cases such as pouring water from one impure well into another, and the intra-Hanafi differences between Imam Muhammad and Abu Yusuf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the basic ruling
Determine what triggers the full pumping obligation: a small or large animal that becomes bloated or disintegrates inside the well. The ruling is that all water must be pumped out (nazh al-ma' kullihi).
Bloating (intifakh) means limbs disintegrate; disintegration (tafasukh) means separation into pieces.
2
Understand the reason (illah)
The reason is that when the animal bloats, its moisture (billa) separates and spreads like a drop of wine, contaminating the entire well. Thus, the ruling is analogized to a drop of wine falling into water.
Also, if a cut body part (e.g., a mouse's tail) falls in, the cut site is not free from impurity, so full pumping is required.
3
Apply the conditional exceptions
If the animal is removed before bloating, no pumping is required because no parts remain. Pumping before removal is futile. If the water dries up before pumping and returns, it remains impure unless the bottom dries, then there are two narrations; the most correct is that it does not return impure if the bottom dries.
Also, the bucket, rope, and hands become pure when the well is purified, due to hardship (haraj).
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute on pouring impure water
When water from an impure well (with a known obligatory amount) is poured into another well, the amount to pump from the second well is based on the greater of the poured amount or the obligatory amount. Imam Muhammad's view: pump the greater. Abu Yusuf has two narrations: pump all water, or pump both the obligatory and poured. The relied-upon position is Muhammad's.
Al-Isbijabi reconciles the narrations by considering whether the poured water is added or not.

And (bloating of an animal or its disintegration) meaning all the water of the well is to be pumped out because of the bloating of the animal that fell into it or its disintegration, absolutely, whether the animal is small or large, like a mouse, a human, or an elephant, because the moisture spreads in the parts of the water, for when it bloats, its moisture separates, and it is liquid impurity, so it becomes like a drop of wine. For this reason, if the tail of a mouse falls in, all the water is pumped out because the place of the cut is not free from impurity, unlike if it is taken out before bloating, because nothing of its parts remains in the water after its removal. Bloating is that its limbs disintegrate, and disintegration is that they separate limb by limb. Similarly, if its hair falls out, it is like bloated. He said in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj: 'If a candle is placed on the place of the cut, only what is obligatory upon the mouse is required, etc.' Branches: Pumping before removing the fallen object is not beneficial because the impurity is the cause, and with its remaining, judgment of purity cannot be made, except if its removal is impossible and it becomes impure, as we have mentioned. If the obligatory amount is not found in the well, then pump what is in it; if water comes afterwards, nothing is pumped from it. If the water disappears before pumping and then returns, it returns impure because the purifier is not found. If a man prays in its bottom and it has dried, it suffices him. Thus in al-Tanjis, but in Fath al-Qadir he chose that it does not return impure, and he stated in the chapter on impurities that there are two narrations, the most correct being non-return, because it is like pumping, as in al-Mi'raj, and its explanation will come if Allah wills. However, the most correct is non-return only when its bottom dries; if it disappears and its bottom does not dry, the most correct is return, as stated in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj. When the well is purified, the bucket, rope, pulley, sides of the well, and the hand of the drawer are purified, because the impurity of these things is due to the impurity of the well, so they are purified by its purification due to hardship, like the jar of wine that is purified secondarily when it becomes vinegar, and like the hand of the one who performs istinja which is purified by the purification of the place, and like the handle of the ewer when there is wet impurity on his hand and he places his hand on it; whenever he pours water on his hand, when he washes his hand three times, the handle is purified by the purification of the hand. If the impurity flows onto something else and then reaches the water, and he pumps it out, all are purified. And it is said that the bucket is pure in respect to this well but not others, like the blood of a martyr which is pure in respect to itself. It is not obligatory to pump out the mud in any of the cases, because the traditions only came regarding pumping water. In al-Mujtaba: 'And whenever something is pumped from the well, the bucket is purified proportionally, and it requires reflection.' In Fatawa Qadikhan: 'The mosque should not be plastered with the mud of the well that has been pumped out, as a precaution.' Then the impurity of the well after removing the mouse and others is severe, then according to what is pumped, it lightens. If the first bucket from a well in which twenty buckets are obligatory is poured into a pure well, twenty buckets are pumped from the second. If the second is poured, ten are pumped, and likewise the third. If the last bucket is poured, a similar bucket is pumped. The basis for this is that the second well is purified by what the first is purified by. If the mouse is removed and thrown into a pure well, and also twenty from the first are poured into it, removing the mouse and pumping twenty buckets is obligatory, because the first is purified by it, so the second is likewise. If the tenth bucket is poured into a pure well, ten buckets are pumped from it in the narration of Abu Sulayman, and in the narration of Abu Hafs it is eleven, which is the most correct. Al-Isbijabi said: 'He reconciled the two narrations: the first is without the poured, the second is with the poured, so there is no difference.' If water from a impure well is poured into another well that is also impure, we consider between the poured and the obligatory in it; whichever is greater suffices the lesser. If they are equal, then pumping one of them suffices. Example: two wells, in each a mouse died. Ten buckets are pumped from one and poured into the other; twenty are pumped. Even if one bucket is poured, likewise. If a mouse dies in a third well, and twenty are poured from one well and ten from the other, thirty are pumped. If twenty are poured from each, forty are pumped. It is appropriate to pump the poured first, then the obligatory in it according to the narration of Abu Hafs. If one bucket from the forty is pumped and poured into the twenty, forty are pumped, because if it were poured into a pure well, it would be pumped likewise, so this is similar. All this is the saying of Muhammad. From Abu Yusuf there are two narrations: in one, all water is pumped; in the other, both the obligatory and the poured are pumped together. It was said to him: 'Muhammad related from you the greater,' so he denied. Similarly, Abu Yusuf said regarding two wells, in each of which a cat fell: one bucket was pumped from one and poured into the other; all its water is pumped in the first narration, because the bucket that was pumped took the ruling of impurity. For this reason, if it touches a garment, it makes it impure and it must be washed, so it becomes like another impurity falling into the well. And only this narration is relied upon in al-Tanjis. It was rebutted in Fath al-Qadir by saying that the reasoning appears only in the previous case where the poured into is pure; if it is impure, then no, because the effect of the impurity of this bucket only appears when it comes upon pure water, and here it comes upon impure water, so its impurity effect does not appear, so the recipient remains as it was, and is purified by removing the obligatory amount. The rebuttal's point is based on what is in al-Mujtaba. Reflect on his statement: (except when its removal is impossible and it becomes impure) by this he excludes the pure essence of impurity. Al-Qahistani said: In al-Jawahir, if a sparrow falls into a well and they are unable to remove it, as long as it is in it, it is impure, so it is left for a period in which it is known that it has transformed and becomes sludge, and it is said a period of six months. End. His statement: (and it requires reflection) meaning
Source pages p. 212

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is a commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq regarding the purification of a well when an animal falls in. The author first states the ruling: if the animal becomes bloated or disintegrated inside the well, all the water must be pumped out regardless of the animal's size. The reason is that when the animal bloats, its liquid impurity (the moisture from its body) mixes with the water, making it like a drop of wine, which contaminates the entire well. Therefore, even the tail of a mouse (if cut) requires full pumping because the cut site is not free from impurity. However, if the animal is removed before bloating, the water is not entirely impure since no part remains. The author also notes that if a candle is sealed over the cut site, only the ruling of a mouse applies (less water?). Then he lists branches (furu'): pumping before removal of the fallen object is useless because the source of impurity remains; if the well lacks the required amount of water, pump what is there and later water does not need pumping; if water disappears before pumping and returns, it returns impure unless the bottom dries—there are two narrations, the most correct being that it does not return impure if the bottom dries. Once the well is purified, the bucket, rope, pulley, and hands become pure automatically due to hardship, as in the case of a wine jar becoming vinegar. The mud at the bottom does not need to be removed. The passage then discusses cases where water from one impure well is poured into another, involving calculations of obligatory pumping amounts. It presents the positions of Imam Muhammad and Abu Yusuf. The author also addresses whether the bucket itself becomes impure: in some views, it is pure only for that well. Finally, the condition 'except when its removal is impossible' is distinguished from the pure essence of impurity. The commentary maintains the Hanafi tradition by citing authorities like al-Siraj al-Wahhaj, Fath al-Qadir, and al-Mujtaba.

Key Terms
انتفاخ (intifakh): Bloating of the animal's body due to decomposition, causing liquid impurity to separate.
تفسخ (tafasukh): Disintegration of the animal into separate pieces.
نزح (nazh): To pump out or remove water from a well as a means of purification.
بلة (billa): Moisture or liquid impurity that separates from the bloated animal.
دلو (dalw): Bucket used to draw water; its purity status is discussed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if an animal bloats in a well, what is the ruling?
A) Only the water surrounding the animal must be pumped.
B) All water must be pumped out.
C) The well becomes permanently impure.
D) The animal must be removed and then 20 buckets pumped.

Key Takeaway
Bloating or disintegration of any animal in a well obligates pumping all water, with special rules for added impure water, and the relied-upon intra-Hanafi view is Imam Muhammad's.

Purifying a Contaminated Well: Bucket Counts and Mixing Rulings
Wells purification rulings with mixing scenarios

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the obligatory number of buckets required to purify a well after a mouse's death, and apply the rule of mixing contaminated well waters to determine the total number of buckets to scoop.

Core Idea
When mixing contaminated well waters, scoop the greater of the poured amount and the existing obligation.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies the Hanafi ruling on purifying a well after a mouse (or similar) dies in it. The number of buckets is based on transmitted traditions, and the school distinguishes between small and large animals. A key principle is introduced for cases where water from one contaminated well is poured into another: you must scoop the larger of the two amounts. This prevents unnecessary repetition and ensures purification.

Guided Path
1
Identify the impurity and its severity
Recognize that a dead mouse in a well makes its water impure. The impurity is initially severe, then lightens as water is scooped. The required number of buckets is wajib based on transmitted traditions.
2
Determine the obligatory bucket number
For a mouse, 20 buckets are obligatory. For a pigeon, 40. These numbers come from athar (traditions) and are part of Zahir al-Riwayah.
Other animals have different numbers, but the passage focuses on mice.
3
Understand the mixing rule
When water from a contaminated well is poured into another contaminated well, compare the amount poured with the amount already obligatory in the receiving well. The greater of the two must be scooped; if equal, scooping either suffices.
This rule applies regardless of whether the incoming water is from a well that already had its obligation scooped or not.
4
Apply to examples
If 20 buckets from a mouse-well are poured into another mouse-well (also 20 obligatory), only 20 need to be scooped (since both are equal). If 10 are poured into one requiring 20, then 20 are scooped (the greater).
The examples in the text illustrate various combinations.
5
Note intra-Hanafi differences
There are two narrations about the exact count when a specific bucket number is poured. Abu Sulayman says exclude the poured amount, Abu Hafs includes it. The reconciliation clarifies there is no contradiction.
The relied-upon position is that of Muhammad (Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani), as stated in the text.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الطهارة غيرها كدم الشهيد طاهر في حق نفسه، ولا يجب نزح الطين في شيء من الصور لأن الآثار إنما وردت بنزح الماء، وفي المجتبى : وكلما نزح من البئر شيء طهر من الدلو بقدره وليتأمل فيه. وفي فتاوى قاضيخان ولا يطين المسجد بطين البئر التي نزحت احتياطاً. ثم نجاسة البئر بعد إخراج الفأرة وغيرها غليظة ثم بقدر ما ينزح تخف، فلو صب الدلو الأول من بئر وجب فيها نزح عشرين في بئر طاهرة ينزح من الثانية عشرون، ولو صب الثاني ينزح عشر وكذا الثالث على هذا، ولو صب الدلو الآخير ينزح دلو مثله، والأصل في هذا أن البئر الثانية تطهر بما تطهر به الأولى. ولو أخرجت الفأرة وألقيت في بئر طاهرة وصب أيضاً فيها عشرون من الأولى يجب إخراج الفأرة ونزح عشرين دلواً لأن الأولى تطهر به فكذا الثانية، ولو صب الدلو العاشرة في بئر طاهرة ينزح منها عشر دلاء في رواية أبي سليمان، وفي رواية أبي حفص إحدى عشرة وهو الأصح . قال الاسبيجابي : ووفق بين الروايتين فالأولى سوى المصبوب والثانية مع المصبوب فلا خلاف ولو صب ماء بئر نجسة في بئر آخر وهي نجسة أيضاً ينظر بين المصبوب وبين الواجب فيها فأيهما كان أكثر أغنى عن الأقل، فإن استويا فنزح أحدهما يكفي . مثاله بئران ماتت في كل منهما فأرة فنزح من إحداهما عشرة مثلاً وصب في الأخرى ينزح عشرون ولو صب دلو واحد فكذلك، ولو ماتت فأرة في بئر ثالثة فصب من إحدى البئرين عشرون ومن الأخرى عشرة ينزح ثلاثون، ولو صب فيها من كل عشرون نزح أربعون، وينبغي أن ينزح المصبوب، ثم الواجب فيها على رواية أبي حفص، ولو نزح دلو من الأربعين وصب في العشرين ينزح الأربعون لأنه لو صب في بئر طاهرة ينزح كذلك فكذا هذا. وهذا كله قول محمد
Book of Purification: Other than that, like the blood of a martyr, it is pure with regard to itself. It is not obligatory to scoop out mud in any case because the narrations only came regarding scooping out water. In al-Mujtaba: Whenever something is scooped from a well, the well becomes pure according to the amount of the bucket; and one should reflect on this. In Fatawa Qadikhan: One should not plaster the mosque with mud from a well that has been scooped out, as a precaution. Then, the impurity of the well after removing the mouse and other things is severe, then according to the amount scooped, it becomes light. So if the first bucket from a well in which twenty (buckets) are obligatory is poured into a pure well, twenty are scooped from the second. If the second is poured, ten are scooped, similarly the third; if the last bucket is poured, a similar bucket is scooped. The basis for this is that the second well becomes pure by that which purifies the first. If the mouse is removed and thrown into a pure well and also twenty from the first are poured into it, it is obligatory to remove the mouse and scoop twenty buckets because the first is purified by it, so too the second. If the tenth bucket is poured into a pure well, ten buckets are scooped from it in the narration of Abu Sulayman; in the narration of Abu Hafs, eleven, and this is the most correct. As-Sabijabi said: He reconciled the two narrations: the first (narration) excludes the poured amount, the second includes it, so there is no contradiction. If water from a contaminated well is poured into another well which is also contaminated, one considers between the poured amount and the obligatory amount in it; whichever is greater suffices and the lesser is dispensed with. If they are equal, then scooping one of them suffices. Example: Two wells, in each a mouse died; ten (buckets) are scooped from one and poured into the other; twenty are scooped. If one bucket is poured, similarly. If a mouse dies in a third well, and twenty are poured from one of the two wells and ten from the other, thirty are scooped. If twenty are poured from each, forty are scooped. It is appropriate to scoop the poured amount then the obligatory amount in it according to the narration of Abu Hafs. If a bucket is scooped from the forty and poured into the twenty, the forty are scooped because if it were poured into a pure well, it would be scooped similarly. All this is the saying of Muhammad.
Source pages p. 213

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the rulings on purifying a well contaminated by a dead animal (like a mouse). The key point is that the number of buckets (dilu) required to purify the well is based on transmitted traditions (athar). For a mouse, 20 buckets are required; for a pigeon, 40. The text also discusses cases where water from a contaminated well is mixed with another contaminated well. The rule is that you must scoop the greater of the two: the amount that was poured in or the amount already required in the receiving well. If they are equal, either suffices. The examples illustrate this principle. The reliance on Imam Muhammad's (Muhammad al-Shaybani) ruling is significant, as his narrations form part of the Zahir al-Riwayah, which is the authoritative core of the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
نزح (nazḥ): The act of scooping or drawing water from a well using a bucket.
فأرة (fa'rah): A mouse; the impurity of its death in a well requires 20 buckets to be removed.
دلو (dalw): Bucket; the standard measure for drawing water from a well.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) 20
B) 40
C) 10
D) 30

Key Takeaway
When mixing water from two contaminated wells, the purification requires scooping the greater of the two amounts; if equal, one suffices.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute: Abu Yusuf vs Muhammad on Mixed Well Water
Intra-Hanafi dispute over scooping quantity when mixing impure well water.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the two narrations from Abu Yusuf and the position of Imam Muhammad on scooping water when impure well water is mixed, and identify the relied-upon position.

Core Idea
Adding impure water to an already impure well does not increase the impurity; the required scoop amount is the greater of the poured or obligatory amount.

This passage explores an intra-Hanafi disagreement: when water from one contaminated well is poured into another, how much must be scooped? Abu Yusuf has two narrations, one requiring all water to be removed, the other requiring both the poured and obligatory amounts. Imam Muhammad holds that only the greater of the two amounts suffices. Through the analysis of the underlying principle—whether the added water introduces a new impurity—the later Hanafi masters favor Muhammad's position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three positions
State Imam Muhammad's position (scoop the greater of poured or required amount) and Abu Yusuf's two narrations (scoop all water; scoop both poured and required).
The first narration of Abu Yusuf is the most stringent.
2
Understand the specific scenario
Two wells, each contaminated by a cat. One bucket is drawn from the first well and poured into the second. The dispute centers on the second well's purification.
The amount required for each well is determined by the animal's size.
3
Analyze Abu Yusuf's first narration reasoning
The drawn bucket has taken the ruling of impurity; if it touches pure water it would make it impure. Therefore, pouring it into the well is like adding a new impurity, requiring all water to be scooped.
This reasoning appears in the narration confined to al-Tanqih.
4
Examine the Hanafi response from Fath al-Qadir
Al-Marghinani refutes that the bucket's impurity only manifests when encountering pure water. Since the receiving well is already impure, no new impurity is introduced; the well is purified by removing its required amount.
The refutation is supported by al-Mujtaba.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
Imam Muhammad's position is the relied-upon view. It is simpler and is preferred by later Hanafi authorities.
The thamarah al-khilaf is significant: one narration may require scooping all water, while Muhammad's requires only the greater of two amounts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهذا كله قول محمد وعن أبي يوسف روايتان في رواية ينزح جميع الماء، وفي رواية ينزح الواجب والمصبوب جميعاً فقيل له : إن محمداً روى عنك الأكثر فأنكر . . وكذا قال أبو يوسف في بئرين وقع في كل منهما سنور فنزح من إحداهما دلو وصب في الأخرى ينزح ماؤها كله على الرواية الأولى لأن الدلو الذي نزح أخذ حكم النجاسة، ولهذا لو أصاب الثوب نجسه ويجب غسله فصار كما إذا وقع في البئر نجاسة أخرى، واقتصر على هذه الرواية في التنجيس. ودفعه في فتح القدير بأن هذا إنما يظهر وجهه في المسألة السابقة وهي ما إذا كان المصبوب فيها طاهرة، أما إذا كانت نجسة فلا، لأن أثر نجاسة هذا الدلو إنما يظهر فيما إذا ورد على طاهر وقد ورد هنا على نجس فلا يظهر أثر نجاسته فتبقى الموردة على ما كانت فتطهر بإخراج القدر الواجب. وجه دفعه عن المسألة ما في المجتبى مبني على هذا تأمل قوله
All this is the saying of Muhammad. From Abu Yusuf there are two narrations: in one narration, he scoops all the water; in another narration, he scoops both the obligatory and the poured amount. So it was said to him: 'Indeed Muhammad narrated from you the greater (amount)', and he denied. Similarly, Abu Yusuf said regarding two wells, in each of which a cat fell: if a bucket is scooped from one and poured into the other, all its water is scooped according to the first narration, because the bucket that was scooped has taken the ruling of impurity. For this reason, if it touches a garment, it makes it impure and must be washed. So it becomes like another impurity falling into the well. He confined to this narration in al-Tanqih. Al-Marghinani in Fath al-Qadir refuted this, stating that this reasoning is clear only in the previous case, where the well into which it was poured is pure. As for when it is impure, no, because the effect of impurity of this bucket only becomes apparent when it encounters a pure thing; here, it encountered an impure thing, so its impurity has no effect. Thus, the receiving well remains as it was and becomes pure by removing the required amount. The refutation of his (Abu Yusuf's) statement from al-Mujtaba is built on this; reflect on his statement.
Source pages p. 213

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Muhammad and Abu Yusuf on how to handle the mixing of water from contaminated wells. Muhammad's position is the one detailed in the previous lesson: you scoop the greater of the poured or required amount. Abu Yusuf has two narrations: one requiring scooping all water, another requiring scooping both the poured and required amounts. The text then discusses a specific case of two wells each with a cat. If one bucket is drawn from a well and poured into the other, according to Abu Yusuf's first narration, all water must be scooped because the drawn bucket is impure and acts like a new impurity. However, al-Marghinani in Fath al-Qadir refutes this, arguing that the impurity of the bucket only has an effect when it encounters pure water; if the receiving well is already impure, no new impurity is introduced, and the well is purified by removing its required amount. This refutation is supported by al-Mujtaba. The relied-upon position is Muhammad's.

Key Terms
سنور (sinnawr): A cat; its impurity in a well requires the same ruling as a mouse? The text does not specify the number, but it is used as an example.
رواية (riwayah): A narration or transmission of an opinion from Abu Yusuf.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) All water
B) 20 buckets
C) 40 buckets
D) 10 buckets

Key Takeaway
When impure well water is mixed with other impure well water, the substance of impurity does not increase; the required scoop quantity is the greater of the poured amount or the well's original obligation.

Exception When Impurity Removal Is Impossible
Explains the exception for impossible removal.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a well when a dead animal cannot be removed and identify the condition for purification.

Core Idea
If removal is impossible, the well water remains impure until the animal fully decomposes into mud.

This lesson addresses a practical exception: what happens when a creature falls into a well and cannot be extracted? The Hanafi school provides a clear ruling: the water is not immediately pure; it must be left until the animal disintegrates. The text estimates this period as up to six months.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Recognise the case: a sparrow (or similar) falls into a well and cannot be removed. The impurity here is the dead animal's body (najis 'ayn).
Distinguish from liquid impurity which is removed by scooping.
2
Apply the condition of impossibility
The ruling hinges on the impossibility of removal. If removal is possible, normal scooping rules apply.
3
State the ruling
As long as the animal remains, the water is impure. Leave it for a period known to allow decomposition into sludge (ham'a).
The text quotes a view: six months.
4
Identify the basis
This is an exception (istithna) to the general rule of scooping. It is based on necessity and the transformation of the impurity.
The ruling is not based on qiyas but on specific transmission.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
